  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_1ac7a24d-5305-46db-8b8f-e095f2158fb1'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);

    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_355643069" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/355643069" />
    <a title="Reynje" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5590906-reynje"><img alt="Reynje" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1473722441p2/5590906.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/355643069?book_show_action=true">Jun 25, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Reynje" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Reynje" href="/user/show/5590906-reynje">Reynje</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer355643069" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2773783323969980770">Having previously read Entangled, I was aware that Cat Clarke is unafraid to take readers to very difficult places in her confronting, intense novels. I knew that Torn would be an emotionally complicated book. But perhaps I wasn’t quite prepared for what a position of discomfort it was about to place me in, or the deeply disturbing implications it would force me to contemplate.<br/> <br/>In Torn, Clarke skilfully taps into the emotional cesspit that accompanies guilt: the consuming dread, self-loathing an</span>
  <span id="freeText2773783323969980770" style="display:none">Having previously read Entangled, I was aware that Cat Clarke is unafraid to take readers to very difficult places in her confronting, intense novels. I knew that Torn would be an emotionally complicated book. But perhaps I wasn’t quite prepared for what a position of discomfort it was about to place me in, or the deeply disturbing implications it would force me to contemplate.<br /> <br />In Torn, Clarke skilfully taps into the emotional cesspit that accompanies guilt: the consuming dread, self-loathing and anxiety. By burdening the reader early on with a dark secret, Clarke effectively forces them into the position of her protagonist, caught between guilt and the instinct for self-preservation. This sense of complicity with the main character is a powerful tool, and it makes her mental and emotional unravelling all the more compelling as the story unfolds. <br /><br />It would be easy to label Torn as a book about bullying and the terrible consequences, but it’s far less clear-cut than simply documenting the actions of perpetrators and victims, or a case of cruelty and revenge. The story is about the complex dynamic between the central characters, and it is made abundantly clear that black and white labels cannot be applied to each individual. Almost all of the characters do horrible things, and the roots of their issues go deep. While the results of their actions may be extreme, the inciting incidents aren’t. The tensions and conflict between the girls are all too familiar and believable, and they are all culpable in some way for its escalation. <br /><br />This is possibly the strongest element of the novel – that while none of the girls are really “likeable” characters (nor do I require this in a book), they’re still compelling. Clarke manages to take a group of people who engage in unsympathetic behaviour, and still make their story emotionally engaging. As each of these flawed characters are more fully revealed, the truth of the situation becomes more muddied, and attributing blame a more complicated exercise. In a way, Torn breaks down the stereotypical concept of the ‘mean girl’, implying rather sinisterly that the capacity for cruelty exists within everyone. <br /><br />This is a difficult book to read. I’ve deliberately avoided discussing the plot, but I can tell you that I felt deeply unsettled throughout, even occasionally nauseous, as I was drawn into the story. While I never fully sympathised with Alice, the protagonist, the vicarious experience of her story was intense. Clarke has an exceptional ability to take disturbing situations, and force the reader to consider the viewpoints of her characters, whether we personally believe them to be right or wrong. It’s almost a feeling of being manipulated, though in an effective, thought-provoking manner, forcing the reader to question everything. Even themselves. <br /><br />In some ways, this reading experience is reminiscent of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/181782829" rel="nofollow noopener">Stolen</a>, especially its atmosphere of mounting anxiety and moral ambiguity. It’s uncomfortable and challenging, a powerful examination of the destructive nature of guilt. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2773783323969980770" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_210178198" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/210178198" />
    <a title="Kylie Simpson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5354304-kylie-simpson"><img alt="Kylie Simpson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1304244503p2/5354304.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/210178198?book_show_action=true">Sep 18, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kylie Simpson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kylie Simpson" href="/user/show/5354304-kylie-simpson">Kylie Simpson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer210178198" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6222951172001848617">Wow, I really dislike Cat Clarke. Not only is she funny and intelligent, but she writes wonderful books that keep you glued to the page until the bitter end. Damn her and her incredible talent. Her characters are both wonderfully real, and credibly flawed, and you find youself relating to them much as you would a friend of a friend. After reading Entangled, with its much loathed protagonist (that i actually loved), Torn was such a change, but equally compelling. I dont like to compare Cat's nove</span>
  <span id="freeText6222951172001848617" style="display:none">Wow, I really dislike Cat Clarke. Not only is she funny and intelligent, but she writes wonderful books that keep you glued to the page until the bitter end. Damn her and her incredible talent. Her characters are both wonderfully real, and credibly flawed, and you find youself relating to them much as you would a friend of a friend. After reading Entangled, with its much loathed protagonist (that i actually loved), Torn was such a change, but equally compelling. I dont like to compare Cat's novels to anything else, but when someone asked me about this, I said it was "Mean Girls meets The Secret History". Doesn't quite do it justice, but my subsequent rave about Torn made it a must read. If you have had enough of the paranormal/supernatural/afterlife/dystopian teen fiction crowding up shelves, Torn is a welcome breath of fresh air. This takes me back to the books I read as a teen, before Edward and Bella and Harry and Ron spawned so many copycats that they created an entire genre. Back to the days when authors recognised that people like to read stories about real characters in real situations. Well done again Cat. Can not wait for book three. </span>
  <a data-text-id="6222951172001848617" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_261137328" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/261137328" />
    <a title="Maria " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5769334-maria"><img alt="Maria " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1600318539p2/5769334.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/261137328?book_show_action=true">Jan 12, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maria " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maria " href="/user/show/5769334-maria">Maria </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer261137328" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7070065578154322453"><i>Alice has a secret.<br/>She has a big secret that is eating her up inside.<br/>She knows something but she couldn’t bring herself to say it.<br/>Something happened to Tara Chambers.<br/>Tara is dead.<br/>Alice knows how she died.<br/>She knows.<br/>But she and three other girls swore that they’ll keep their mouth shut about what happened.<br/>Then Tara’s brother Jack enters the picture.<br/>Alice likes Jack.<br/>Her conscience is killing her.<br/>Jack told her he likes her.<br/>Alice was restless and confused.<br/>Will her conscience win her over and tell Tar</i></span>
  <span id="freeText7070065578154322453" style="display:none"><i>Alice has a secret.<br />She has a big secret that is eating her up inside.<br />She knows something but she couldn’t bring herself to say it.<br />Something happened to Tara Chambers.<br />Tara is dead.<br />Alice knows how she died.<br />She knows.<br />But she and three other girls swore that they’ll keep their mouth shut about what happened.<br />Then Tara’s brother Jack enters the picture.<br />Alice likes Jack.<br />Her conscience is killing her.<br />Jack told her he likes her.<br />Alice was restless and confused.<br />Will her conscience win her over and tell Tara’s brother the truth or will she keep the truth hidden forever so that they wouldn’t get in trouble?</i><br /><br /><br /><b>Torn</b> was simple and direct to the point.<br />This book tackled not only the human nature of self preservation but also how human conscience works.<br /><br />The main character Alice was torn between doing the right thing and protecting herself and her friends.<br />She knew that if she opens her mouth they all would get in trouble.<br />Someone ending up dead because of a stupid prank was serious stuff even if what happened was an accident.<br />Alice was the perfect example of how the author used both the human’s concept of self-preservation and the power of the human conscience.<br />I mentioned earlier that this book tackled self-preservation.<br />Alice and her friends kept silent on what really happened to Tara because they needed to protect themselves.<br />They needed to stir the spotlight away from themselves.<br />They needed to not let people know that they had something to do with it because if it happens they were going to be facing a major major problem. <br />They wanted to preserve themselves even if it means that they have to lie to everyone about what happened.<br /><br />I wanted to slap Alice a couple of times throughout this book because she was a total pushover. <br />She knew that what Cass and Polly were planning was wrong but she didn’t argue strong enough.<br />She doesn’t know how to stand up for herself.<br />There were a lot of things I didn’t like about Alice which is why I loved this book.<br />It shows us how a teenager would react if given the same situation.<br />She was imperfectly perfect for this book.<br />It felt real.<br />Alice felt real.<br />Tara felt real.<br />All the characters seemed so real to me.<br />Reading this book was like watching a movie.<br />All the characters have dimension and meaning.<br />The book was not all about Alice and Tara and what happened.<br />All the characters had their part to play and they made this book great.<br />All of them were flawed but great.<br /><br /><b>Torn</b> was written in a way that you’ll relate to each and every one of the characters.<br />The emotions were raw and powerful.<br />This book has so much going on in it.<br />There are tons of things to learn from this book one of which is to make sure you treat other people in a way you’d like to be treated.<br />I honestly don’t blame them for wanting to get back at Tara because I feel that she deserved it too but what happened here was just too wrong.<br />Tara was not all that bad.<br />I actually felt sorry for her not because she died but because she got carried away with popularity that she threw away a good friendship.<br /><br />Lies, Secret, Guilt, Love and Friendship made this book.<br /><br />Would I recommend it?<br /><br />Absolutely!<br /><br />I give this <b>4.5 stars!</b><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7070065578154322453" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText4727790148833215583" style="display:none"><i>Four girls. One dead body.</i><br /><br />If that doesn't sell you immediately, then I don't know what will.<br /><br />This is <i>such</i> and underhyped book. I was completely blown away the first time I read this at thirteen and it has aged remarkably well - I am still in awe of just how insanely <i>gripping</i> it is and how convincingly Cat Clarke writes as a contemporary teenager.<br /><br /><i>Torn</i> is as deeply disturbing as it is heartfelt with an enthralling plot, a sarcastic bite and a bloody good twist.     <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_180101695" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/180101695" />
    <a title="Laura " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5401175-laura"><img alt="Laura " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1336931153p2/5401175.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/180101695?book_show_action=true">Jun 27, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Laura " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Laura " href="/user/show/5401175-laura">Laura </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer180101695" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4598342432195529458">Okay, Cat Clarke. I don't know whether to fall at your feet and worship you, or hunt you down and punch you in the face! But to explain why I'm feeling so torn (he he... that was unintentional but see what I did there?) would be very spoilerific. So let's get back to the whole reviewing part of this review. <br/><br/>I read and reviewed Clarke's first book, Entangled, a short while back. You can read my gushy praise of that incredible book here. I adored it. I adored it so much I gave it five stars (after</span>
  <span id="freeText4598342432195529458" style="display:none">Okay, Cat Clarke. I don't know whether to fall at your feet and worship you, or hunt you down and punch you in the face! But to explain why I'm feeling so torn (he he... that was unintentional but see what I did there?) would be very spoilerific. So let's get back to the whole reviewing part of this review. <br /><br />I read and reviewed Clarke's first book, Entangled, a short while back. You can read my gushy praise of that incredible book here. I adored it. I adored it so much I gave it five stars (after a brief hostage situation with one of the stars anyway... For the record, Cat Clarke does not negotiate with blogorrists!). So, when I saw that Clarke was having a little competition on her blog and the prize would be the very first ARC of Torn, I had to enter. <br /><br />As luck would have it, I won! I did a proper little happy dance around my kitchen when I found out (though it seems half of Twitter knew before I did, as it was through them that I heard the good news) and proceeded to sit by my mailbox and await my delivery. It arrived and I squeeled a li'l bit. <br /><br />Then life, as it does, got in the way for a little while. You know how it is. Shit happens and sometimes the rug get whipped out from under our feet. Have I ever mentioned that I have the ugliest feet in the universe? But anyway... After I got the rug back in place beneath my hooves and nailed it down for good measure, I finally got around to reading Torn this afternoon. I finished it about ten minutes ago and just had to review it as soon as I possibly could. But how to do this without spoiling the ride for the rest of you?! <br /><br />Let me begin by saying this: Cat Clarke is the best author of YA I have read this year. In Torn, just like in Entangled, she creates characters who you will recognise. I could see aspects of Alice in myself. The way she remembers fishing for parental compliments after parents' evenings. The way she gets annoyed if someone uses more than three dots in an ellipsis. But it wasn't just the protagonist that was painted with these evocative hues of realism. <br />- The "queen bee-atch", Tara, and the best-buddy Cass, both reminded me of times when my tongue was, perhaps, a little too sharp. <br />- The adorable Jack had trouble expressing the emotions most important to him in just the same verbally-vomiting way that I do. <br />- Emo, music-obsessed and antisocial Rae had a few familiar traits.<br />- But most of all, Alice's English teacher, Daley, reminds me a lot of me! A fairly newbie teacher who wants to save her pupils and who hopefully, remembers school well enough to see through the charades that the young-uns like to put on. <br /><br />Cat Clarke is really good at creating flawed characters. I don't just mean the trivial flaws that are often prevalent in YA, (you know what I mean: "My hair is too frizzy...", "My boobs are too small", "I'm a social outcast..."). No no no. Clarke goes for the big flaws which are far more real. She creates characters who act in all the wrong and improper ways when faced with drama and calamity. They fu...dge up. They don't just mess up because it's good for the story, or because it adds necessary conflict. Her characters mess up in all the ways that real people mess up. We chicken out. We swear and get horny. We act selfishly. We hurt people to console ourselves. We bitch. We get jealous. We lie. <br /><br />We do all of these things and yet whenever we read a story, don't we see ourselves as the hero? Despite all our own flaws, we all want to be the one to save the Nakatomi Towers, or defeat the Alien, or take on the Terminators. Clarke gives us protagonists who sometimes do bad things but who also want their "Yippy-ki-yay-Get-away-from-her-you-bitch-Come-with-me-if-you-want-to-live" moment. This, to me, is real and it therefore makes me really care about and empathise with her characters. <br /><br />Which is great. Except Cat Clarke likes her realistic narratives so much that sometimes she has to go and put her characters in painful and impossible situations. She hurts them and, through her razor sharp prose, cuts us too! Deeply. <br /><br />So darn you, Cat Clarke! You've made me cry for the second time, and for that I kind of want to throttle you and beg you to take it easy on your poor protagonists. At the same time, you've made damn sure that I will go out and buy every single book you ever write, because you're bloody terrific! Ours is to be a love-hate relationship, I think! He he he. <br /><br />Lx</span>
  <a data-text-id="4598342432195529458" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13736893380694741275">I wanted to read this so much that I ordered it from the UK. Not one single library near me owned it. I think I was drawn in by the very pretty cover and the blurb on the back. Unfortunately, the blurb on the back is only about one quarter of the book. I expected a "We Know What you Did Last Summer" type read, and what this is.....well, it's kind of a messed up love story. <br/>I think they should have called this book "How Not to Be A Friend", and it had the potential to be an awesome book of realis</span>
  <span id="freeText13736893380694741275" style="display:none">I wanted to read this so much that I ordered it from the UK. Not one single library near me owned it. I think I was drawn in by the very pretty cover and the blurb on the back. Unfortunately, the blurb on the back is only about one quarter of the book. I expected a "We Know What you Did Last Summer" type read, and what this is.....well, it's kind of a messed up love story. <br />I think they should have called this book "How Not to Be A Friend", and it had the potential to be an awesome book of realistic fiction with a tinge of horror and instead it is filled with four girls who are so unbelievable in their actions that the reader cringes. <br />How is one supposed to understand someone who plays a part in killing a girl, pretends she is innocent, and then dates the dead girl's brother? Is the reader to believe that a character would be MORE upset over her father dating again than killing a person? I wanted to reach into this book and smack the hell out of Alice. <br />I wanted Polly to dangerous and Cass to have a real reason to do what they did. I wanted closure. <br /><br />I think it's me. I grew up on Heathers, and thought this was going to have more meat to it. <br />At the same time, Cat Clarke can write. The proof is in the fact that I didn't stop reading. I just didn't like where this story went (or rather, where it didn't go). I wanted depth. I also, after getting to the very end wanted to see some sort of punishment for what was terrible, terrible behavior. <br /><br />So future Torn readers, be advised that this is not a thriller. </span>
  <a data-text-id="13736893380694741275" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText15731524392475153425" style="display:none">I really don't know how to sum up this book. I truly, truly hated it. The main reason for me giving this book 1 star was the complete lack of plot and any kind of build up, a very weak romantic sub-plot, no originality and total predictability, and the single most frustrating, selfish and weak characters I've probably ever read about. I think 'cringey dialogue' and 'weak plot' probably sum up this book for me, and I honestly wanted to throw the main character and her equally dull romantic counter-part into the fiery depths. The one thing really that kept me reading was the conclusion that this book would inevitably come to, and I actually would be intrigued to read about, but alas, the book ended just as it was about to happen. What a surprise. Really would not recommend to anyone.</span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it

<span id="freeTextContainer1429020602454938775"><b>Actual rating 4.5</b><br/><br/><b>Pre-reading:</b><br/>I added this to my wishlist because I am a visual person :D <br/>Had the cover saved on my laptop for weeks now as "beautiful cover" and I thought I might check the blurb today - absolutely INTRIGUING! Can't wait to buy this babe...<br/><br/><b>Post-reading.</b><br/>Okay whew.<br/>I stayed up till way past midnight to finish this and that's something that hasn't happened quite often lately.<br/><br/>I love it when books mess with my feelings, when I physically <i>feel</i> something whilst reading, that way I know I</span>
  <span id="freeText1429020602454938775" style="display:none"><b>Actual rating 4.5</b><br /><br /><b>Pre-reading:</b><br />I added this to my wishlist because I am a visual person :D <br />Had the cover saved on my laptop for weeks now as "beautiful cover" and I thought I might check the blurb today - absolutely INTRIGUING! Can't wait to buy this babe...<br /><br /><b>Post-reading.</b><br />Okay whew.<br />I stayed up till way past midnight to finish this and that's something that hasn't happened quite often lately.<br /><br />I love it when books mess with my feelings, when I physically <i>feel</i> something whilst reading, that way I know I've been really sucked up into the story and somewhat emotionally attached. yay.<br />I think Cat Clarke's writing style is perfect for this kind of story as it's not distracting in itself but pushes to the point (does that make sense) and she let's actions speak, not words.<br /><br />The whole plot is just so genius really, simple things happening that have devastating consequences, but it's all logic still and well-thought through, loose ends all got tied up in my opinion.<br />I never thought a book basically about guilt could be this mesmerizing but yes, it is, and I even felt uneasy simply reading about the happenings.<br />A very solid read, if you ask me.<br />I'd like to go into more detail really, but I fear that would be too spoilery.<br />I recommend this if you enjoy books by Sara Shepard and emotional suspense.<br /><br />If you've read this: I always feel like Alice has probably least to do with it all (and Rae maybe too) but that she blames herself just as much but really it is sooooo not her fault because she had basically no clue about anything going on. grmphf.</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer385653272" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17047097420636588225">I don't really know how to assess this book. It was very complex... It's got me into a right mess, it's like someone took the inside of my head and shook it like a tube of M&M's. Countless moments while reading I put the book down and just bathed in my shock. My favorite thing about this book is the fact that it's not predictable. I can normally sniff out the ending a mile off, but this book is definitely in a league of it's own in that venue. However, one of my least favorite things about this </span>
  <span id="freeText17047097420636588225" style="display:none">I don't really know how to assess this book. It was very complex... It's got me into a right mess, it's like someone took the inside of my head and shook it like a tube of M&amp;M's. Countless moments while reading I put the book down and just bathed in my shock. My favorite thing about this book is the fact that it's not predictable. I can normally sniff out the ending a mile off, but this book is definitely in a league of it's own in that venue. However, one of my least favorite things about this book is how Clarke would make it seem like these heavy issues were not that big of a deal.  Like when Rae died, no one seemed to batter an eyelid, for some reason that death disturbed me more.  I also found the 'romance' in this book incredibly annoying and the 'ghost' too. I also feel like the author took the easy way out by just randomly cutting it towards the end, like a cliffhanger effect; I feel it would've been too difficult to write a proper full ending, since there's no happy way to finish things. Although, it does give you a good think about popularity, so-called friendships and revenge.<br />Should we judge people by the good in their hearts or the horror of their acts? </span>
  <a data-text-id="17047097420636588225" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

I loved this one particularly because she talks about something close to my heart and something I struggle with daily.<br/>I always fly through her books because I just can't get enough of them her writing style is so easy to get in to and keep you there.<br/>Can't wait for another one :)</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1915977436" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6900430665959922523"><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/photos/1480153363p8/1781219.jpg' width='600' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><a href='http://amagicalworldofwords.blogspot.co.za/' rel='nofollow noopener'>A Magical World Of Words</a><br/><br/>Ooooh *shivers*<br/>I really enjoyed this book.<br/><br/><br/>It wasn't a nice story in the slightest, but <b>it was decently written and constantly entertaining.</b> I literally could <i>not</i> put the book down. I was utterly gripped, terrified, and freaked out. <b>It was vividly and intimately haunting, and the subject matter was agonising.</b> It was a probing look into the lives of school girls made even more horrifying by the fact that they were my age. It was creepy and frightening for me to read about t</span>
  <span id="freeText6900430665959922523" style="display:none"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/photos/1480153363p8/1781219.jpg" width="600" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><a href="http://amagicalworldofwords.blogspot.co.za/" rel="nofollow noopener">A Magical World Of Words</a><br><br>Ooooh *shivers*<br>I really enjoyed this book.<br><br><br>It wasn't a nice story in the slightest, but <b>it was decently written and constantly entertaining.</b> I literally could <i>not</i> put the book down. I was utterly gripped, terrified, and freaked out. <b>It was vividly and intimately haunting, and the subject matter was agonising.</b> It was a probing look into the lives of school girls made even more horrifying by the fact that they were my age. It was creepy and frightening for me to read about their experiences all the while knowing I could be in their place. <b>It was chilling and real, and it was gut-wrenching.</b> <br>On a side note, suicide and murder were mentioned frequently. This was a very dark story. <br><br><b>The plot wasn't original. And the characters</b> - while vivid - <b>were stereotypical and predictable.</b> Yet they moved me, and they felt real to me, and in the end the stereotypes weren't as annoying as they might have been.<br><b>.The dialogue wasn't great, and the story took predictable and unoriginal turns.</b> Still, I thought it drastically improved after the incident of Tara's death; before her death, it was much more cliche and the foreshadowing seemed forced. Afterwards, the characters became much more fully realised, and I loved seeing all their secrets come to light. It allowed me to better understand their previous actions, and I loved watching them as they revealed their true colours. <br><br><b>.I didn't like any of the characters.</b> I could relate to Alice a bit, and at first I rather liked the teacher, Daley, but ultimately there was no one I was rooting for; if you can put it like that. Towards the end, however, I did really grow to like Danni. She was strong and interesting, and I enjoyed seeing her true character show itself after Tara's death.<br><b>I wasn't a big fan of the romance.</b> It was predictable, lukewarm, and boring. <br><br><br>I feel like I should explain to you why this review is largely negative but I'm still giving the book 4 flowers ;) <br>Well, I enjoyed reading it.<br><br><i>
  <b>Torn</b>
</i> <b>was gripping, terrifying, entertaining and tragic. It certainly had its flaws, but I really "enjoyed" getting lost in the horrifying, gut-wrenching, dark world of teenage lies, love, insecurities, and fears.</b></span>

<div id="review_644156223" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/644156223" />
    <a title="Jacqueline Escobar" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15648685-jacqueline-escobar"><img alt="Jacqueline Escobar" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1590532318p2/15648685.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/644156223?book_show_action=true">Jun 17, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jacqueline Escobar" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jacqueline Escobar" href="/user/show/15648685-jacqueline-escobar">Jacqueline Escobar</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15648685-jacqueline-escobar?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15648685-jacqueline-escobar?shelf=disappointed">disappointed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer644156223" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3626779072224355488">"Four girls. One dead body." I was so intrigued by these two sentences. I had to read it. It sounded so different from any YA book I'd read before. Four girls caught up in a murder, who wouldn't want to read that? Sadly it didn't live up to what I thought it would be.<br/><br/>The first part of the book was good. I loved the setting in the beginning at the funeral. The mystery at the beginning was played out well. It made you want to read on and find out what happened and how exactly these four girls were</span>
  <span id="freeText3626779072224355488" style="display:none">"Four girls. One dead body." I was so intrigued by these two sentences. I had to read it. It sounded so different from any YA book I'd read before. Four girls caught up in a murder, who wouldn't want to read that? Sadly it didn't live up to what I thought it would be.<br /><br />The first part of the book was good. I loved the setting in the beginning at the funeral. The mystery at the beginning was played out well. It made you want to read on and find out what happened and how exactly these four girls were involved. However, after we find out what happened the plot line started to get really weak. I expected there be more. But no, it got turned into a very weak love story. The whole idea of "Tara's ghost" to kick start the story was weak. It was just so dull. There was no climax. By the middle of the book I just didn't care anymore. I hated that it was turned into a "romantic story." That's not what I wanted to get from this story. I felt like the romance was the main plot of the book, and Tara's whole death was gradually put to the side and used as a way to move on Jack and Alice's relationship. <br /><br />The ending, for me felt like it was rushed. It's almost as if Cat Clarke was so focused on Jack and Alice, that she forget she had a murder to deal with, like "oh yes, let me just cram this in there quickly." I wanted to know more. What happened after Alice did what she did? What were the consequences on all the other girls?<br /><br />I wasn't particularly a huge fan of the writing either. The short, choppy sentences, I did not like. It was like walking through honey. It didn't do anything for me. It just made the story drag out even more.<br /><br />As for the characters, I felt nothing towards them. I understand they're not meant to be likeable, but I would have at least like to felt just a little ounce of emotion. I felt there was nothing there. Their grief and guilt didn't feel real to me. They were all just a bit bland, expect Rae. The only one I liked, who hardly said anything in the entire book. So much more could have been there with her, instead of just giving her the ending she had.<br /><br />Overall, the idea for the plot was irresistible. Sadly, it lacked the potential of being such a great and interesting story. So much more could have been done.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3626779072224355488" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_339890657" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/339890657" />
    <a title="Samantha" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6241881-samantha"><img alt="Samantha" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1452736538p2/6241881.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/339890657?book_show_action=true">May 31, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Samantha" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Samantha" href="/user/show/6241881-samantha">Samantha</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6241881-samantha?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer339890657" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6476028491739658774">Cat Clarke is one of the those rare YA authors that actually write truthful books. Books that really hit at your emotions yet feel as though they were written purely for the teen market. You could easily compare her to the likes of Courtney Summers, Laurie Halse Anderson and Joanna Nadin all of whom write brilliantly written young adult fiction.<br/><br/>Torn is Cat’s second novel after the wonderfully written Entangled. Torn tells us the story of Alice, a teenagers from London who is hiding a dark and te</span>
  <span id="freeText6476028491739658774" style="display:none">Cat Clarke is one of the those rare YA authors that actually write truthful books. Books that really hit at your emotions yet feel as though they were written purely for the teen market. You could easily compare her to the likes of Courtney Summers, Laurie Halse Anderson and Joanna Nadin all of whom write brilliantly written young adult fiction.<br /><br />Torn is Cat’s second novel after the wonderfully written Entangled. Torn tells us the story of Alice, a teenagers from London who is hiding a dark and terrible secret. Haunted by the ghost of her old friend Tara and seriously questioning those around her Alice struggles to come to terms with Tara’s death and who really caused it.<br /><br />The book is, simply put, a fantastic read. The character of Alice of the page and you feel so sympathetic to her even after what she involved in. The whole narrative captivates from the start and has you gripped to the book until you finally finish. I was so hooked by this book that I read the whole thing in just a few hours.<br /><br />Cat’s way of writing is simple but at the same time so full of emotions that really pulls at your heart. I found myself loving Alice’s character and really wanting her to find closure over Tara’s death. Secondary characters such as Alice’s best friend Cass, the quiet Rae, more-than-she-seems-to-be Polly and Tara’s borther Jack all have thier own voices. You find yourself laughing, crying or wanting to kill them because of their characteristics and voices.<br /><br />The ending was well thought out and had me desperate for just one more chapter and you really do keep guessing over the whole truth of Tara’s death right up until the end of the book.<br /><br />I really enjoyed this book and actually cannot wait to read it again. Well done Cat, a truly brilliant book. <br /><br />Original Review: <a href="http://harmony-everlark.tumblr.com/post/25965056128/my-edit" rel="nofollow noopener"> Here </a></span>
  <a data-text-id="6476028491739658774" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_459851654" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/459851654" />
    <a title="Zoe and the Edge" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14304864-zoe-and-the-edge"><img alt="Zoe and the Edge" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1352171027p2/14304864.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/459851654?book_show_action=true">Nov 20, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Zoe and the Edge" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Zoe and the Edge" href="/user/show/14304864-zoe-and-the-edge">Zoe and the Edge</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14304864-zoe-and-the-edge?shelf=squeaky-clean">squeaky-clean</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14304864-zoe-and-the-edge?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14304864-zoe-and-the-edge?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14304864-zoe-and-the-edge?shelf=psychological">psychological</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14304864-zoe-and-the-edge?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14304864-zoe-and-the-edge?shelf=siblings">siblings</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer459851654" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17694984144258194925"><i>
  <b>It’s too weird to think about – how death seems to rewrite all the rules.</b>
</i><br/><br/>That about sums up the book. Some strange and scary shit goes down and all you can do is keep turning the pages to find out how it ends. <br/><br/><i>
  <b>Alice - My heart is clearly stupid. It has a tendency to get overexcited for no reason.</b>
</i><br/><br/>Alice's gentle sarcasm and storytelling sucked me in fast. I don't know what it is about her, I just liked her tone. She's a normal, extremely average girl. <br/>There's something so sinister and subt</span>
  <span id="freeText17694984144258194925" style="display:none"><i>
  <b>It’s too weird to think about – how death seems to rewrite all the rules.</b>
</i><br /><br />That about sums up the book. Some strange and scary shit goes down and all you can do is keep turning the pages to find out how it ends. <br /><br /><i>
  <b>Alice - My heart is clearly stupid. It has a tendency to get overexcited for no reason.</b>
</i><br /><br />Alice's gentle sarcasm and storytelling sucked me in fast. I don't know what it is about her, I just liked her tone. She's a normal, extremely average girl. <br />There's something so sinister and subtle about her story that I didn't realise I couldn't put the book down until it was too late. <br />Alice asks some good questions with the twisted situations she finds herself in. The plot stretches out in a different direction than I originally thought it would. <br />As the story moves on, it starts getting a bit psychologically convoluted and all kinds of mind-effing delicious. I mean, who's really the bad guy? <br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<i><b>I’m going to have to spend Saturday with Jack, knowing that a) I as good as murdered his sister, and b) he does not want to kiss me. A normal person might not be able to think these thoughts simultaneously. A normal person might be more concerned about a) than b). Clearly there is something very, very wrong with me.</b></i><br /><br />It adds something infinitely intriguing to have the roles of grief and guilt mixed up. Most of the times when a story revolves around a death, the characters grieve and feel that they were responsible when really they weren't. But in this one the characters <i>are</i> responsible and aren't grieving and that puts a totally different spin on it. <br /><br /><b>The Romance</b><br />I didn't like it at first. Main reason obviously being that it was doomed from the start. But as it went on, Jack and Alice just felt more and more right to me. Even their names together have a nice ring to it. <br /> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>

<div id="review_198797343" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/198797343" />
    <a title="Sya" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3579145-sya"><img alt="Sya" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1525200688p2/3579145.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/198797343?book_show_action=true">Aug 15, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sya" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sya" href="/user/show/3579145-sya">Sya</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer198797343" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17860278359447478225">At first glance, the storyline of Torn – teenage prank gone wrong – may seem familiar, even hackneyed but to dismiss it as such would be a grave mistake. While other writers may have been tempted to use this premise as the basis for an angst ridden mystery, Cat Clarke rather deftly uses it as a basis for a fascinating study of guilt, grief and the constantly shifting currents of teenage hierarchy. However, Clarke doesn’t veer entirely away from mystery and thriller territory here and at times To</span>
  <span id="freeText17860278359447478225" style="display:none">At first glance, the storyline of Torn – teenage prank gone wrong – may seem familiar, even hackneyed but to dismiss it as such would be a grave mistake. While other writers may have been tempted to use this premise as the basis for an angst ridden mystery, Cat Clarke rather deftly uses it as a basis for a fascinating study of guilt, grief and the constantly shifting currents of teenage hierarchy. However, Clarke doesn’t veer entirely away from mystery and thriller territory here and at times Torn is very frightening (not to mention quietly gruesome) - fans of Edgar Allan Poe would do well to take a look at this modern day riff on the themes he so often wrote on in an equally creepy fashion.<br /><br />As with her debut, Entangled, Torn is not an entirely easy read and this is largely to do with Clarke’s ability to get inside the head of teenage girls. Clarke captures vividly the reality of teenage interaction – illustrating perfectly the ease at which the bullied become bullies and vice versa. Her writing is captivating and extremely moving – the final scene between Alice and her father is sure to engender more than a few tears. Clarke is also mistress of the literary sucker-punch, her sparse yet haunting prose often deliverying a sly one-two, leaving readers gob-smacked. With Torn, Cat Clarke has cemented her place as an author to watch. This is the contemporary title that others in the UK (not to mention America) need to beat and I can honestly say that there are few titles that I have read that are as skilfully written. Pick up a copy as soon as you can.<br /><br />(full review available at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.mountainsofinstead.com">www.mountainsofinstead.com</a>)</span>
  <a data-text-id="17860278359447478225" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText11178109465442300902" style="display:none">I'm trying to remember a time when I enjoyed a book as much as I enjoyed this one. A time when I actually read an entire book in only one day. This book was amazing. I have only just finished reading it and my emotions are all jumbled and mashed up in a state of never wanting to part from reading this book. <br /><br />The main character Alice, I loved her. I actually loved her. She was so perfect even though she was kind of messed up with everything that had happened. I think it's the way the author really made me feel connected with her and her emotions. She's torn between doing the right or doing the wrong thing in order to protect herself and her "friends." This book was perfect from begging to end. The writing flowed perfectly and had me completely wrapped up in the story. <br /><br />Ending spoiler:<br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[The end of the book completely left me sitting here thinking "nooooooooooooooooooo" because I did not want it to end like that. I wanted Alice to stay with Jack even though it was messed up; I wanted them to live happily ever after, but obviously that couldn't happen. I wanted her to bury her secret and lead a happy life. Although weirdly enough, the fact that the ending was not what I wanted it to be made me love the book even more. Maybe it was the fact that she chose to be brave and admit to what had happened, maybe that <i>was</i> her happily ever after. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /></span>

<div id="review_1409790309" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1409790309" />
    <a title="Zara" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/28262919-zara"><img alt="Zara" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1483876507p2/28262919.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1409790309?book_show_action=true">Jan 06, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Zara" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Zara" href="/user/show/28262919-zara">Zara</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28262919-zara?shelf=physical-copies-i-own">physical-copies-i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28262919-zara?shelf=reread">reread</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28262919-zara?shelf=loving-the-cover">loving-the-cover</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28262919-zara?shelf=4-stars">4-stars</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1409790309" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6216001548955054741"><blockquote>
  <i>"A funeral without a body is like a wedding without a bride, or a groom."</i>
</blockquote><br/>This is my second read of <i>Torn</i> and I <b>still ended up feeling like I've been punched in the gut</b>. <br/><br/>From the moment <i>Torn</i> starts, we are told about the mystery surrounding Tara's death and while the details surrounding her death are revealed quite early, they become more <b>murky, disturbing and messed up</b> as the story progresses. <br/><br/>The characters in <i>Torn</i> might be <b>stereotypical</b>, there's the mean girls, the emo chick and the social </span>
  <span id="freeText6216001548955054741" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>"A funeral without a body is like a wedding without a bride, or a groom."</i>
</blockquote><br />This is my second read of <i>Torn</i> and I <b>still ended up feeling like I've been punched in the gut</b>. <br /><br />From the moment <i>Torn</i> starts, we are told about the mystery surrounding Tara's death and while the details surrounding her death are revealed quite early, they become more <b>murky, disturbing and messed up</b> as the story progresses. <br /><br />The characters in <i>Torn</i> might be <b>stereotypical</b>, there's the mean girls, the emo chick and the social outcast, but the way that they act and the emotions that they go through are <b>real</b>. None of the characters in <i>Torn</i> are likable. They are <b>flawed</b> and their actions are <b>disturbing</b>. However, while I felt like screaming at the characters to just do the right thing, <b>I understood why they weren't doing it</b>. The characters in <i>Torn</i> <b>might not be likable</b>, but their stories are <b>extremely compelling</b>. A lot of it boils down to the fact that Cat Clarke is <b>able to get into her characters heads</b> and shows how every little thing that they go through impacts them. <br /><br />I'm <b>extremely conflicted about the romance</b> in <i>Torn</i>. The relationship between Alice and Jack, Tara's little brother, is <b>destined to fail</b> from the moment that it starts <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[because Alice played a role in his sister's death <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, but they have one of those <b>cute first-love teenage romances</b>. The romance <b>isn't special or unique</b>, but every moment that Jack and Alice were together <b>made me worry</b> because I was just waiting for her to tell him the truth.<br /><br />The <b>best part</b> about <i>Torn</i> is the <b>analysis of grief, guilt, anxiety and human self-preservation</b> as well as the <b>emotional effects and consequences of the characters actions</b>. Ghost Tara was an <b>interesting manifestation</b> of Alice's trauma and guilt.<br /><br />I understand that <i>Torn</i> is mostly about Alice dealing with the events that occurred, the aftermath and the choices that come with it, but I <b>didn't like the open ending</b>. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I wanted to see the consequences of Alice's, Cass's, Polly's and Rae's actions. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br /><br />Cat Clarke is <b>not afraid to put her characters through the most</b>. <i>Torn</i> made me <b>confront disturbing situations</b>. <i>Torn</i> put me, the reader, in an <b>uncomfortable situation</b>. <i>Torn</i> <b>made me think</b>. <i>Torn</i> is <b>filled with powerful, raw and painful emotions that tore me to pieces</b>. <br /><blockquote>
  <i>"Maybe this is how madness works. At first you're worried you're going crazy, but in the end you don't even care. You embrace it; it's the only thing you've got left." (Alice King)</i>
</blockquote> </span>
  <a data-text-id="6216001548955054741" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2376372638" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12457245906405723620">So often when I'm reading a Cat Clarke book, I'll read it in one sitting. They're entertaining, easy, accessible, and this one was no exception. Cat's books are kind of like domestic thrillers, just YA, basically. <br/>I guess my problem moving forward with her writing is that I have zero emotional connection to any of her plots or characters. I don't know if that's important to Cat when writing, but it's important to me when reading - EVEN if it's a thriller!! I don't think I can honestly say I've e</span>
  <span id="freeText12457245906405723620" style="display:none">So often when I'm reading a Cat Clarke book, I'll read it in one sitting. They're entertaining, easy, accessible, and this one was no exception. Cat's books are kind of like domestic thrillers, just YA, basically. <br />I guess my problem moving forward with her writing is that I have zero emotional connection to any of her plots or characters. I don't know if that's important to Cat when writing, but it's important to me when reading - EVEN if it's a thriller!! I don't think I can honestly say I've ever given a book over four stars or over if I haven't felt emotionally invested in the outcome of SOME element, if not the entire thing.<br />So yeah I think these stories are easy to read, some better than others, and quite fun in places, but I just struggle to invest in them. If that's not a necessity for you as a reader and entertainment is more important then I think you'd definitely enjoy Cat Clarke's books, this one included.</span>

<div id="review_657632749" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/657632749" />
    <a title="Matilda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4437023-matilda"><img alt="Matilda" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1372932788p2/4437023.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/657632749?book_show_action=true">Jul 03, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Matilda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Matilda" href="/user/show/4437023-matilda">Matilda</a>
      </span>

          added it




        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4437023-matilda?shelf=i-own">i-own</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer657632749" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14309050633444711531">I tried to write a review for this book and when I was finally pretty much finished and satisfied with it, my laptop shut down and I lost everything. This has happened to everyone and it never gets any less frustrating no matter how many times it happens. Ugh. So here I go again - my second try at writing a decent review; I can guarantee it won't be half as good as the first I wrote, so apologies in advance.<br/><br/>The idea behind Torn is what made me want it to read it so much. Alice King goes on a sch</span>
  <span id="freeText14309050633444711531" style="display:none">I tried to write a review for this book and when I was finally pretty much finished and satisfied with it, my laptop shut down and I lost everything. This has happened to everyone and it never gets any less frustrating no matter how many times it happens. Ugh. So here I go again - my second try at writing a decent review; I can guarantee it won't be half as good as the first I wrote, so apologies in advance.<br /><br />The idea behind Torn is what made me want it to read it so much. Alice King goes on a school trip to Scotland with her best friend Cass and is expecting it to be boring. It's the type of trip that will probably be full of outdoors-y type activities, the kind that very few teenagers enjoy or look forward to. The concept is that on this trip, Alice, Cass and two others - Polly Sutcliffe, a complete social outcast and Rae Morgan, a girl who fits the stereotype of an 'emo', prefers to be by herself, preferring music over people - are placed into a cabin together, along with another girl: Tara Chambers, the most popular girl in school.<br /><br />Tara Chambers is the girl that everyone seems to hate, yet wants to be at the same time. She is beautiful and powerful through being so popular, with a group of friends who seem to worship the ground she walks on in a disciple-like manner. However, she <i>is</i> cruel to those she views as 'lower' than her on the school social ladder.<br /><br />And on the trip, one night, the girls come up with the idea of getting Tara back after humiliating one of them; they are seeking revenge, just wanting to scare her and make her pay. But when this 'prank' goes wrong, the girls lives are literally changed forever. Nothing can ever make this mistake right and they must learn to live with the guilt that will haunt them for everyday of their lives afterwards.<br /><br />As I mentioned, the idea behind Torn is what made me want to read it. I was so anticipated for it because the concept is just so incredible. There would be so many ways to go with this. And my expectations must have been too high, because I felt a bit let down with this book.<br /><br />Firstly, the actual 'accident' that occurs isn't that dramatic. I'm not saying that it wouldn't be completely horrific if it genuinely did happen in real life, just that to read in a book, it wasn't as bad as I'd expected and it could have been written completely differently, with something different happening, and therefore I would have found it more entertaining and interesting to read. <br /><br />Another thing I disliked was the main character. I didn't completely hate her or anything, she seemed nice enough and everything, but I just didn't find her or the others very believable, purely for the fact that if this situation had happened to someone, realistically, they would be acting in a completely different way.<br /><br />You would not feel a little bit sad and guilty and get over it. You would most likely feel consumed with guilt and worry. And even if you had like these girls managed in a way to kind of resolve the situation, you'd still be constantly fearing someone finding out about what <i>really</i> happened to the girl you accidentally killed.<br /><br />I just feel like the characters didn't act in a very believable way. They all seemed to cope with it pretty well. <br /><br />Another thing I disliked was that once the 'accident' had occurred (which is pretty early on in the book, may I add) I was just waiting to see what the girls would do in the end. Everything in between seemed a bit pointless and boring to read. <br /><br />Lastly the ending was alright; however, like I did from the whole book, I expected more - I expected something bigger and better and more entertaining to read.<br /><br />Anyhow, I'm not saying Torn is a bad book. The idea behind it is great and it wasn't entirely dull and lifeless. I didn't mind reading it but then again I definitely wasn't blown away.<br /><br />I just feel like someone else could have taken this idea and wrote it differently and it could have been better.<br /><br />That is all.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14309050633444711531" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_227993442" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/227993442" />
    <a title="Sarah" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3344685-sarah"><img alt="Sarah" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1388694025p2/3344685.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/227993442?book_show_action=true">Oct 27, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sarah" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sarah" href="/user/show/3344685-sarah">Sarah</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3344685-sarah?shelf=read-in-2012">read-in-2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3344685-sarah?shelf=books-i-own-print">books-i-own-print</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3344685-sarah?shelf=signed">signed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3344685-sarah?shelf=british-author">british-author</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer227993442" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9148924087590944993">When Alice and her best friend Cass get stuck sharing a cabin with the school queen bee Tara and social outcasts Polly and Rae they know they're not going to enjoy their school trip to Scotland. But after a plan to get revenge on Tara goes horribly wrong things take a devastating turn for the worse and nothing will ever be the same again.<br/><br/>I loved Cat Clarke's debut novel Entangled when I read it last year so I couldn't wait to get my hands on her latest book Torn. I'm happy to say that this book </span>
  <span id="freeText9148924087590944993" style="display:none">When Alice and her best friend Cass get stuck sharing a cabin with the school queen bee Tara and social outcasts Polly and Rae they know they're not going to enjoy their school trip to Scotland. But after a plan to get revenge on Tara goes horribly wrong things take a devastating turn for the worse and nothing will ever be the same again.<br /><br />I loved Cat Clarke's debut novel Entangled when I read it last year so I couldn't wait to get my hands on her latest book Torn. I'm happy to say that this book was just as gripping as I expected it to be. Cat manages to write such realistic teenagers that it takes you straight back to your school days. I remember going on a similar school trip and having the same feelings of horror about the activities that Alice did which instantly helped me to connect with her. Luckily for me all of my classmates made it back to school in one piece which is more than can be said for Alice and her friends.<br /><br />Alice is the kind of girl that most of us are able to relate to, she isn't one of the most popular crowd but she isn't quite at the bottom of the social pecking order either. Instead she hovers somewhere in the middle of the two groups and although she would desperately like to be more popular she isn't blind to the faults of the mean girls who run the school social scene. I love the way you slowly unravel more of Alice's past and as you do you discover some things about her previous friendship with the school queen of mean Tara that will surprise you. Torn really does show you just how far teenagers will go to change their social standing and just how brutal school politics and relationships can be.<br /><br />Alongside Alice you really get to know some of the other main characters and although the accident was horrific and their actions afterwards are unforgivable you can't help but feel sorry for the way they ended up in that situation. The scariest thing was how believable it all was - I was left thinking that I wouldn't be shocked to find that this was based on a true story (although hopefully it wasn't lol).<br /><br />Torn is a book about grief, about bullying and the long term effects it can have, it is also about guilt and how that emotion can completely change a person. At times it is a dark and difficult book to read and it is one that leaves you with plenty to think about. At the same time there are also funny moments, there is an adorable romance that captures the excitement of first love perfectly and there are lessons to be learnt about the importance of friendships and not betraying those who have always been there for you. Torn is an engrossing read and one that I couldn't put down - definitely a book I'd recommend to fans of YA thrillers and mysteries.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9148924087590944993" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_496536496" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/496536496" />
    <a title="Sarah Elizabeth" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7591340-sarah-elizabeth"><img alt="Sarah Elizabeth" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1328957304p2/7591340.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/496536496?book_show_action=true">Jan 05, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sarah Elizabeth" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sarah Elizabeth" href="/user/show/7591340-sarah-elizabeth">Sarah Elizabeth</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7591340-sarah-elizabeth?shelf=bought-2013">bought-2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7591340-sarah-elizabeth?shelf=read-2013">read-2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7591340-sarah-elizabeth?shelf=made-me-laugh">made-me-laugh</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7591340-sarah-elizabeth?shelf=read-with-abbie">read-with-abbie</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7591340-sarah-elizabeth?shelf=amazon-sale">amazon-sale</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7591340-sarah-elizabeth?shelf=british-books">british-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer496536496" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9303169248098375211">(Source: I own a copy of this book.)<br/>Alice and Tara used to be friends, but now Tara is popular, and Alice isn’t. <br/>When they are forced to share a cabin with 3 other girls whilst on a school trip, Alice isn’t impressed at Tara’s behaviour towards one of the other girls, and although she initially doesn’t want to, she joins in on a prank on Tara that goes horribly wrong.<br/>Can the girls live with the secret of what happened to Tara? Can Tara’s family move on without her? And could something have been </span>
  <span id="freeText9303169248098375211" style="display:none">(Source: I own a copy of this book.)<br />Alice and Tara used to be friends, but now Tara is popular, and Alice isn’t. <br />When they are forced to share a cabin with 3 other girls whilst on a school trip, Alice isn’t impressed at Tara’s behaviour towards one of the other girls, and although she initially doesn’t want to, she joins in on a prank on Tara that goes horribly wrong.<br />Can the girls live with the secret of what happened to Tara? Can Tara’s family move on without her? And could something have been done to save Tara?<br /><br /><br />I was a little wary of reading this one because I wasn’t the biggest fan of this author’s other book ‘Entangled’, but I’m so glad I did because I really enjoyed the mystery in this one, and it also made me laugh!<br /><br />Alice was an interesting character, although at times I was a little worried how she didn’t lose more sleep over what had happened. I did feel bad for her, and for the other girls, but I really didn’t understand how they could live with the guilt of what they had done.<br /><br />I liked the storyline in this one, and I thought the mystery element was done well. I really enjoyed trying to work out what would happen, and every time a new problem came up I couldn’t help but laugh at the characters expense!<br />There were some interesting little twists in this that I liked, and again I liked the humour. It’s a bit difficult to share some of the more humorous moments with you because of spoilers, but I really did find myself laughing at this book!<br /><br />There was some romance in this book, which while good also had a little twist to it, and was very much on the edge of how clever of a decision this was for Alice. I did enjoy the romance though, even when I thought it was risky.<br /><br />I liked the mystery in this book most of all though, and it was this that kept me reading. I did predict where Tara was going to end up, but I thought that was pretty obvious. I thought the tension over the secret and what would happen was good though, and way better than entangled!<br />The ending was also pretty good, although I did think it would have been nice to have seen a bit more about what happened to Alice and Co. at the end. The ending was satisfactory though, even though we were left wondering about some things, and if there was a sequel I would definitely read it.<br />Overall; a good YA mystery.<br />8 out of 10<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9303169248098375211" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
