    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_205052569" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/205052569" />
    <a title="Cat" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2319016-cat"><img alt="Cat" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1483371941p2/2319016.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/205052569?book_show_action=true">Sep 04, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cat" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cat" href="/user/show/2319016-cat">Cat</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Fans of Cathy MacPhail, Catherine Forde and Kevin Brooks</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2319016-cat?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer205052569" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer427974420895865655">Lucky enough to get an early review copy of this, I looked forward to reading it with curiosity. Having read Clarke's first novel, Entangled and really appreciated the twists and turns it provided, I wondered what she could do with her second offering. It did not disappoint. Now I should make a few things clear. I got this as a freebie from the publisher, I know that some bloggers and reviewers who get publisher freebies ooze gratuitously all over the books, regardless of whether they are a bit </span>
  <span id="freeText427974420895865655" style="display:none">Lucky enough to get an early review copy of this, I looked forward to reading it with curiosity. Having read Clarke's first novel, Entangled and really appreciated the twists and turns it provided, I wondered what she could do with her second offering. It did not disappoint. Now I should make a few things clear. I got this as a freebie from the publisher, I know that some bloggers and reviewers who get publisher freebies ooze gratuitously all over the books, regardless of whether they are a bit shit or not. I am not one of those, because, not only am I a bookseller but I also run book clubs for children and teenagers and there is one thing I have learned about children and reading...you cannot pretend to like something. They will know you lied. And even if they didn't, it is wrong to lie, especially to kids. So I don't. I also happen to know Cat Clarke and I would be doing her a serious disservice if I pretend to like something she had written that was a bit sucky. So there.<br /><br />Torn is not sucky, Torn is excellent. Like Entangled, Cat has taken teenage girls and brought out the best and the worst in them. She has understood their psyche and their motivations and confusions and concocted a psychological thriller that keeps the pages turning. As with Entangled, the first chapter, whacks you round the face with the unexpected and her endings, whilst possibly predictable are actually realistic, hence the possible predictability and I appreciate that, for there aren't always happy endings in life, nor should there be, otherwise how would we learn about coping? I prefer this to Entangled actually. I'm not sure why. Still thinking about this. I also found myself likening Clarke's work to Cathy MacPhail's and Catherine Forde's, and actually, when I think about it, with a smattering of Kevin Brooks thrown in. Edgy, nail-biting, unexpected, psychological, with a smattering of well timed humour. Brilliant.</span>
  <a data-text-id="427974420895865655" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_238077427" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/238077427" />
    <a title="Corinne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4470060-corinne"><img alt="Corinne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1352054170p2/4470060.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/238077427?book_show_action=true">Nov 21, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Corinne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Corinne" href="/user/show/4470060-corinne">Corinne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4470060-corinne?shelf=crime-murder-sleuthing">crime-murder-sleuthing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4470060-corinne?shelf=romance-a-o-love">romance-a-o-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4470060-corinne?shelf=ghosts-a-o-spirits-a-o-revenants">ghosts-a-o-spirits-a-o-revenants</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4470060-corinne?shelf=ebooks">ebooks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4470060-corinne?shelf=school-a-o-university-life">school-a-o-university-life</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4470060-corinne?shelf=almost-favourites">almost-favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4470060-corinne?shelf=coping-with-loss">coping-with-loss</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4470060-corinne?shelf=stand-alone">stand-alone</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer238077427" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8513792322836591956">It took me quite a long time to finish this novel and I'm that kind of person, who stops reading a book as soon as it gets boring or annoying. So normally this is a bad sign for my rating, but in this case I really had to stop reading it because I dreaded the ending and wanted to prolong coming to the end as long as possible. Obviously it didn't work out since I'm writing this review *g* I won't tell you what's going to happen then, so don't be afraid. This is one of these stories that will stay</span>
  <span id="freeText8513792322836591956" style="display:none">It took me quite a long time to finish this novel and I'm that kind of person, who stops reading a book as soon as it gets boring or annoying. So normally this is a bad sign for my rating, but in this case I really had to stop reading it because I dreaded the ending and wanted to prolong coming to the end as long as possible. Obviously it didn't work out since I'm writing this review *g* I won't tell you what's going to happen then, so don't be afraid. This is one of these stories that will stay in my head for quite some time and thus I wanted to write a small review, because it really deserves it!<br /><br />On the whole I prefer fantasy books and although there is a ghost girl in Torn, the focus of Cat Clarke's novel is definitely YA fiction and she delivers it without cheesy &amp; teary dialogs, sentimental lines and most of all without any shortcuts and defined stereotypes! One can really feel and understand the inner turmoil of Alice and the best part of this book was definitely the last conversation between her with Polly and her father too! The author really made the balancing act to avoid this black-and-white murderer versus victim scenario. All the girls involved in this tragic incident that let to the death of one of them are shown as victims but also as having wronged someone else with the intent to hurt this person, too. Especially bullying and mopping in school in connection with the feeling of insecurity during adolescence is one of the major themes and after finishing this one, I'm still unsure who is really to blame for the murder that occurred. Alice, Rae, Cass or Polly or even Tara (the victim) herself? Hard to say, so go ahead, read it and tell me if you think it was really murder or just an accident because Cat Clarke doesn't give a clear answer in my mind.<br /><br />By the way, I gave it 4 out of 5 stars because everybody can imagine how it's going to end and there was no real surprise or unexpected twist in it.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="8513792322836591956" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_643848935" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/643848935" />
    <a title="Beth (bibliobeth)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5858624-beth-bibliobeth"><img alt="Beth (bibliobeth)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1540072118p2/5858624.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/643848935?book_show_action=true">Jun 17, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Beth (bibliobeth)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Beth (bibliobeth)" href="/user/show/5858624-beth-bibliobeth">Beth (bibliobeth)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer643848935" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6007961160819167178">Having read Cat Clarke's debut novel Entangled and really enjoying it, I was excited to read this, her second book. Now I know I've only read two of her books, but I'm guessing that Clarke doesn't like to shy away from difficult or intense subjects! Our main character Alice, is heading off on a school trip to Scotland with her best friend Cass, but ends up being stuck in a cabin with two typical teenage misfits, Polly and Rae, and the most popular (and horrible) girl in the school Tara. Things g</span>
  <span id="freeText6007961160819167178" style="display:none">Having read Cat Clarke's debut novel Entangled and really enjoying it, I was excited to read this, her second book. Now I know I've only read two of her books, but I'm guessing that Clarke doesn't like to shy away from difficult or intense subjects! Our main character Alice, is heading off on a school trip to Scotland with her best friend Cass, but ends up being stuck in a cabin with two typical teenage misfits, Polly and Rae, and the most popular (and horrible) girl in the school Tara. Things go drastically wrong when they decide to teach Tara a lesson after a particularly spiteful incident, but things don't exactly go according to plan...<br /><br />Back in the present day, Alice is having a hard time coming to terms with what has happened, and is suffering from the fact that she can't talk to anyone about it. I think the author did a wonderful job here of letting the reader into the secret quite early on so we experience all the guilt-ridden emotions that Alice does, and feel the complexity of the situation which does not seem to offer any quick or easy resolution. I also loved the close and loving relationship Alice had with her father, her mother having died of cancer several years previously, it seemed to make the situation more despairing as she feared his disappointment. All the characters in this book are written well, and although they may not necessarily be likeable, they are real - warts and all. Clarke has a real talent for engineering people that you can believe in and care about, even in a negative way. If an author can make you dislike a character so much, doesn't that mean they've done their job properly after all to spark that emotion in you?<br /><br />There's no way I'm going to give the ending away but have you ever put a book down and just said Aaaargh?!<br /><br />Please see my full review at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.bibliobeth.wordpress.com">http://www.bibliobeth.wordpress.com</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="6007961160819167178" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('+35mTOOZA5oJnjfb1qhV5Tmg+hwpoVl6nT8GQEA8CIR89m4Eg1l1hFc3b9bdti9o71a1seRnNskW65hJ+z9uYg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('t/8dzu1SgkUOgih58PP8S/MdX0qyyLvtXkDdRJemJk0wdxWGjZL0W1ArcHT77YbGJesQ538O1F7VlENNLKVAqw==')})
  }
